Sun Ke Arrives in Shanghai Yesterday Morning　Firmly Denies Returning South to Sweep Tombs　Attends Wu Chaochu Memorial Committee 113

Sun Ke, President of the Legislative Yuan, arrived in Shanghai from Nanjing yesterday morning. At about 9:00 AM, he and his wife went to the Shanghai Sanatorium Hospital on Robegen Road to treat her old illness. Nie Kaiyi Returns to Shanghai Yesterday　Stranded Airplane Towed Back to Shanghai Yesterday 114

Shenshi News Agency reports that the China Aviation aircraft went missing. Yesterday, the company dispatched another aircraft to scatter reward leaflets and continue the search in the vicinity of Jintang Mountain and Yuxingnao, but there were still no results as of 6:00 PM in the evening. The Sekos aircraft stranded at the Zhenhai Estuary was towed back to Shanghai by Nie Kaiyi yesterday with a tugboat and is now at the Longhua Repair Factory for repairs. According to Nie Kaiyi, despite three days of careful searching along the coast, there was still no clue. Yesterday, the company's manager, Dai Enji, convened a meeting of experts and technicians to discuss further search methods and plans to send several more aircraft to search for the whereabouts this morning. As of last night, there was still no evidence that the passengers on the missing plane were ordinary businessmen or had other business. All parties still consider it a suspicious clue. The Shanghai-Guangdong route is temporarily suspended due to the missing aircraft. The company will convene a board meeting in the coming days to discuss solutions and is rumored to order new aircraft from the United States to restore the Shanghai-Guangdong route. According to the company's statement yesterday, there are no plans to suspend the route. The company is actively planning to add various facilities to the route to ensure safety. Other routes are operating as usual and have not been affected in any way.

Ministry of Finance　Establishes Currency System Research Committee　Office Located at the Central Bank, Xu Kan to Prepare 115

The Ministry of Finance has established a Currency System Research Committee to study currency system reform matters. Zhang Gongquan and fourteen others have been hired as members, and letters of appointment have arrived in Shanghai. The first meeting will be held in Shanghai to officially establish the committee. Details are as follows.

Appointed Committee Members 116

The Ministry of Finance has hired fourteen currency system research committee members, including national banking and money industry leaders Zhang Gongquan, Wu Daquan, Qian Xinzhi, Zhou Zuomin, Chen Guangfu, Bei Songsun, Hu Bijang, Tang Shoumin, Song Ziliang, Hu Mengjia, Xu Xinliu, Qin Runqing, Qu Zuhui, and Shen Yuanding. Xu Kan, Director of the Currency Department, has been designated as an ex officio member.

About to be Established 117

A reporter from Xinsheng News Agency visited the committee members yesterday and learned that the Ministry of Finance's letters of appointment arrived in Shanghai the day before yesterday. The Ministry of Finance has dispatched Xu Kan, Director of the Currency Department, to conduct preparations in Shanghai. It has been decided that the office will be located in the Central Bank on the Bund. The first committee meeting will be held soon to announce the official establishment. The date of the meeting has not yet been determined because committee member Qin Runqing has not returned from Ningbo, and Zhou Zuomin and others are in other locations.

Dispatch Personnel for Investigation 118

The Currency System Research Committee is tentatively composed of fifteen members. After its establishment, several more leaders from the banking and money industry in various regions will be invited to join as members. The Ministry of Finance has hired Li Fusun as a consultant to investigate the currency systems of various countries in order to serve as a reference for China's currency system reform. It is reported that the date of Mr. Li's departure will be determined after the Currency System Research Committee is established.

Announcement of Regulations 119

The Ministry of Finance has announced the regulations of the Currency System Research Committee as follows: Article 1: The Ministry of Finance has established a Currency System Research Committee to study currency system reform matters. Article 2: The Currency System Research Committee shall have several members, selected and appointed by the Minister of Finance, who shall designate one member as the Chairman. Article 3: Meetings of the Currency System Research Committee shall be chaired by the Chairman. Article 4: The Currency System Research Committee shall have one Secretary-General and two Secretaries, with several staff members appointed by the Minister of Finance. Article 5: The Currency System Research Committee shall study the following matters: ㈠ Matters concerning the adoption of the gold standard, ㈡ Matters concerning the silver standard currency, ㈢ Matters concerning various old currencies, ㈤ Matters concerning subsidiary coins, ㈤ Matters concerning the crackdown on private minting, ㈥ Matters concerning the improvement of mint factories, ㈦ Matters concerning the transportation and regulation of local silver and copper coins, ㈧ Matters concerning paper money, ㈨ Matters concerning the crackdown on private issuance of paper money, ㈩ Matters submitted by the Minister of Finance for discussion. Article 6: Members of the Currency System Research Committee may propose motions for discussion regarding the items listed in Article 5. Article 7: Resolutions of the Currency System Research Committee shall be submitted to the Minister of Finance for adoption and implementation. Article 8: Detailed rules for the Currency System Research Committee shall be determined separately. Article 9: These regulations shall take effect from the date of promulgation.

Shanghai Citizens' Association for Promoting National Products Declaration　Support Chairman Chiang's Order　Stop Unauthorized Strikes and Work Stoppages 122

The Shanghai Citizens' Association for Promoting National Products deeply laments that labor-management disputes occur frequently among its factory members, which are not beneficial to either party or may escalate beyond control. This not only affects the factories themselves but also endangers social order. The Standing Committee previously instructed the Planning Department to design countermeasures to eliminate disputes and seek welfare. Now, after reading Chairman Chiang's order to stop unauthorized strikes and work stoppages, the association is deeply gratified for the entire national products industry. Yesterday, the Standing Committee decided to issue a declaration to enthusiastically support the order. The declaration is excerpted as follows: "Promoting national products is the legacy of the Premier's peaceful struggle to save China, and it is especially the basic principle of saving the country during the current national crisis. National products factories, adhering to this spirit, endure pain and hardship and strive to produce in the hope of completing the task of national revival in the process of industrial development. However, in recent years, due to social unrest, national misfortunes, and the economic recession in rural areas, they have been operating hard and barely supporting themselves. They are also constrained by the dumping of foreign goods and affected by the surge in labor unrest, resulting in huge losses and a precarious situation, leading to the trend of industrial decline and factory bankruptcy. This not only reduces the country's due production but also endangers social order. The harm is so severe that it is like entering a point of no return. The national products industry is originally a matter of shared prosperity and mutual dependence for both labor and management. Factories should care for their workers, and workers should work hard, overcome difficulties together, and strengthen the national foundation. The aim is to concentrate national products to save the country, avenge national humiliation, and resist foreign aggression."

"Now, labor-management disputes arise from time to time, causing both sides to sacrifice and feel pain. Moreover, the disputes have escalated beyond control, causing factories to shut down and become unsustainable, leading to an increasing number of unemployed people and creating opportunities for foreign goods to sell well. The association witnesses this dangerous situation and feels great pain. We respectfully read Chairman Chiang's order to stop unauthorized strikes and work stoppages, which hits the nail on the head, eliminates the source of trouble, benefits the country and the people, and is deeply beneficial. We hereby express our utmost sincerity, lead all factory members to enthusiastically support the order, and, under the guidance of party and government agencies, intensify the national products movement, strive to produce, realize the Premier's legacy, and revive the nation. This declaration is hereby made."

Municipal Chamber of Commerce Cables Ministry of Finance　Protesting U.S. Increase in Sesame Import Tax 123

The Municipal Chamber of Commerce yesterday cabled the Ministries of Foreign Affairs and Finance, stating, "On the 12th of this month, we received a letter from the Grain, Oil, and Cake Industry Association stating, 'We received a letter from Ji Yuantang stating that we received a joint letter from Grain Store Yuanhe Ren and others stating that domestic sesame has always been mainly sold to countries such as the United Kingdom and the United States. In recent years, the same economic recession has occurred abroad, so foreign trade is only about one-tenth of what it was in previous years. We now receive telegrams from foreign merchants stating that the U.S. government proposes to increase the sesame import tax to five cents per pound. According to recent prices, selling to foreign firms is only worth seven yuan in national currency per 100 catties. If the U.S. tax rate is applied, it would be equivalent to more than 20 yuan in Chinese currency per 100 catties. This policy is tantamount to rejecting Chinese goods imports and cutting off Chinese merchants' sales channels. Please discuss and come up with relief measures, etc.' After discussion, we believe that this matter concerns international trade and is of great importance. Please forward the letter to the Municipal Chamber of Commerce and cable the Ministries of Finance and Foreign Affairs to strongly urge the U.S. government,' etc. At the same time, we also received a letter from the Bean and Rice Trade Association with the same content. Upon investigation, domestic sesame is not in great demand domestically and is mostly sold to the United Kingdom and the United States. In the past, the value was 12 to 13 yuan per 100 catties, and imports were tax-free. In recent years, the price has gradually declined and is on the verge of collapse. According to the current market price of sesame sold abroad, including the domestic customs tax, it is worth about 7 yuan per catty. Counting shipping costs, it is worth only 113 yuan per ton. If the U.S. government's policy of increasing the import tax to five cents per pound is implemented, then at 2,000 pounds per U.S. ton, it would be an additional 100 U.S. dollars per ton. Assuming a U.S. exchange rate of 35 yuan, it would be equivalent to 285.7 yuan in Chinese currency, which is 2.5 times the current value. The decline of China's rural areas has reached its extreme. The way to revival is not limited to one aspect. Smoothing sales channels and increasing value are the most important tasks. Although sesame is a by-product, the annual exports are not small and have a relationship with the rural economy, which is not a trivial matter. The current sharp drop in prices has already hit farmers hard. If sales channels are cut off due to the U.S. government imposing heavy taxes, the disaster will be even more unbearable. The permission to forward the letter is especially requested for you to promptly cable the Ministry of Finance and Foreign Affairs, requesting the U.S. government to uphold the spirit of coexistence and co-prosperity and revoke the aforementioned motion. We eagerly await your purchase, etc.' We have received the letter. Upon investigation, China's international trade has always seen exports of agricultural products and imports of manufactured goods. The annual trade deficit is already very large. Recently, foreign agricultural products have turned to China as a major import, while China's exports have been affected by the economic depression and heavy taxes, and are obstructed everywhere. In the past two years, the magnitude of the trade surplus has broken the highest record since the opening of mutual markets. If we do not seek to remedy the situation urgently, the people will be impoverished and the wealth will be exhausted, which can be expected in the near future. The association's request to consult with the United States to reduce taxes is a necessary procedure, but each country's increase in taxes has its own position, and tariff autonomy is also its internal affairs. Commercial requests based on virtue and righteousness may not be very effective. The method of addressing the root cause seems to be to predetermine a sliding scale of taxes on each country's special products exported to China, which can be raised or lowered at any time, as a countermeasure. (Omitted in the middle) The matter concerns saving the declining trend of international trade and is not limited to the local interests of the industry. How should we carefully plan for countermeasures? It is appropriate to cable your ministry for review and approval to provide assistance."

Xiang Songmao's Encoffining Today　Five Continents Pharmacy Closed for One Day 131

City Chamber of Commerce's Letter to the Customs Administration Regarding Extending the Deadline for Tax Refunds on Re-levied Taxes 134

The City Chamber of Commerce sent a letter to the Customs Administration yesterday, stating: "To the esteemed Customs Administration, we received a letter on the 13th of this month from the Hub North San Shan Fu Ning Guild, stating that the Fujian Puppet People's Government is re-imposing consolidated taxes. Previously, the Consolidated Tax Bureau had approved that within three months of the re-imposition, the original tax receipts and sub-bills of lading along with the re-imposed tax receipts could be submitted to the bureau for a tax refund. However, the goods transported to Fujian are not only sold near the provincial capital; the majority are distributed to northern and western Fujian. These areas have been plagued by bandits and military operations in recent months, and the remote locations have even been cut off from transportation. Information could not be exchanged for one or two months, resulting in most tax receipts being delayed due to transportation obstructions and difficulties with postal delivery, making it impossible to submit them on time. Having previously expressed these difficulties, the Shanghai Municipal Flour Guild requested the Consolidated Tax Bureau to extend the deadline by three months, but the reply stated that the matter was related to general cases and could not be handled accordingly. However, all the procedures for the tax receipts that have been sent are complete; only the dates are slightly past the deadline. If they are deemed invalid according to the regulations, the losses would be too heavy, and the reasons for the delay are due to special obstructions and not intentional delay. It seems that special consideration should be given. We are now submitting one hundred and thirty-one original tax receipts, twenty-four re-imposed tax receipts, seventy-three sub-bills of lading, and nine Fujian customs documents, totaling four thousand two hundred and seventy national currency units re-imposed, for your esteemed association to review and collect. We hope that you will submit them to the Ministry of Finance on our behalf, requesting that the tax bureau be instructed to handle the overdue tax receipts that have already been sent with flexibility, approve the tax refund, and extend the deadline for the re-imposed tax receipts of the Fujian Puppet People's Government by three months to alleviate the difficulties of merchants. We earnestly hope for your assistance," the letter stated. Upon receiving this, we have reviewed that the original intention of allowing the submission of various documents within three months of the re-imposition to request verification and tax refund from your esteemed administration was to maintain the consolidated tax system, ensuring that taxes would not be re-imposed after the initial tax. Therefore, the stipulation of the deadline should not conflict with this main purpose. The intention of your esteemed administration in setting a three-month deadline was merely to provide merchants with sufficient time to handle the matter. If the deadline is exceeded, it would seem that merchants are too negligent regarding their own rights, and merchants should bear the blame for the error, and your esteemed administration would no longer have the responsibility to protect them. This is the underlying intention. However, the distribution of goods in northern and western Fujian, after the removal of the provincial pretender government, was further complicated by the progress of bandit suppression military operations, leading to transportation disruptions and a lack of communication for one or two months. This situation could not have been foreseen when your esteemed administration set the deadline, and it was also beyond the merchants' ability to remedy, with no negligence on their part. Approving an extension of the deadline is precisely to maintain the spirit of not re-imposing consolidated taxes. The matter is special and does not impede general cases. We request that your esteemed administration approve the request for handling. As for the various tax receipts attached by the guild that have just been sent, the dates may be slightly different, and it is due to military obstruction. We request that you first verify and approve the tax refund to avoid unexpected losses. We are publicly grateful. All the various tax receipts and customs documents have been separately extracted into a list and attached to this letter. We hope that your esteemed administration will verify and handle them and reply accordingly."

City Chamber of Commerce Letter to the Post Office Regarding Improving Tax Standards for Medicine Packages 136

The City Chamber of Commerce sent a letter to the Post Office Tax Collection Department yesterday, stating: "To the esteemed Post Office Tax Collection Department, on the 13th of this month, we received a letter from the Shanghai New Pharmaceutical Industry Association, stating that a member, the Sino-French Pharmacy, wrote that when sending parcels, the Post Office Tax Collection Department used the original drug price list submitted by the China-America Pharmacy to the Customs last year as the basis for ordering taxes based on the sales price on that list. Although they repeatedly explained, they were not listened to, and there was a strong tendency to detain the goods if they did not comply. Under these circumstances, considering the unreasonableness of these people, they had no choice but to painfully pay the tax. Considering that this matter concerns all colleagues in the industry and the future is long, the harm is unimaginable, they sent a letter requesting assistance. The prices of imported goods not only vary from morning to night, but also the finished medicines of various countries are no exception. This is a normal change in commerce. How can the market price of one company in the same industry last year be applied to the goods of this year? Especially since the market price of this industry is even more different in the past two years, how can they be compared? Moreover, the selling price and the estimated price have always been fixed, and they cannot be viewed as the same. Now, the estimated price that they are being forced to revise is much higher than the current selling price for many items. How can merchants bear this kind of tax payment method? They plan to ask your esteemed association to negotiate on their behalf," the letter stated. Upon review, the matters mentioned by the pharmacy are indeed factual. Correspondingly, we are sending a letter requesting your esteemed association to send a letter to the Post Office Tax Collection Department, arguing based on reason. This is our earnest hope. Based on this, the market price of medicines changes from time to time, which is a common practice in general commerce. The estimated tax for postal packages should be based on the current value and accurately estimated, which is sufficient to show fairness. Now, your department is using the original drug price list submitted by the China-America Pharmacy to the Customs last year as the basis for collecting postal tax on medicine packages from the Sino-French Pharmacy, which is excessively higher than the current market price. How can this be used as the standard for tax collection? Correspondingly, we are sending a letter stating the situation, hoping that your esteemed department will take note of it. In the future, the estimated price of medicine packages should be based on the actual market price at the time of mailing, without overcollection, to maintain commerce. We earnestly hope for your assistance, etc."

Wu Tieshan's Seventieth Birthday Celebration 137

Lawyer Wu Guotai, also known as calligrapher and painter Wu Tieshan, has reached the age of seventy and resides at No. 79 Dajing Road, Xiaobeimen. His virtuous wife, Madam Ji, is of the same age. They have a large family, with four sons, eighteen grandchildren, and one great-grandchild. His four sons, Chenggong, Chengjiang, etc., held a seventieth birthday celebration for their parents yesterday at the Brick and Ash Guild Hall in Jinjiafang, Fangbang Road. Many figures from the political, business, legal, and calligraphy and painting circles of the city came to offer their congratulations, including Wu Tiecheng, Wang Yiting, Jiang Yiping, Yao Wenshou, and hundreds of others. Those who came to congratulate gave commemorative porcelain bowls with the inscription "Husband and Wife with Matching Eyebrows, Children and Grandchildren Around the Knees, Four Generations in the Same Hall," as well as carved bamboo chopsticks and other items. The banquet began at 8:00 PM, with lively toasting and various entertainments, and the celebration ended late into the night.

Coffins Exposed in the County Ordered to be Buried by a Deadline 141

The Shanghai County Government, considering that coffins exposed in the county are both unsightly and a hindrance to hygiene, County Magistrate Pan issued an order yesterday instructing the district and township chiefs to conduct a strict investigation and urge the families of the deceased to move the coffins for burial. A public notice was also issued to the public stating that if there are coffins exposed, the families of the deceased must bury them all by the end of June.

The Case of Le Zhenbao's Kidnapping: The Main Culprit is the Owner of a Car Company, Also Involved in Two Other Kidnapping Cases. The Police Added Charges, and the Trial Was Rescheduled. 142

Le Zhenbao, owner of Taichang Wood Shop on Nanjing Road, was kidnapped by bandits at the intersection of Yuyuan Road and Hede Road at 9:30 AM on December 9th, 1932, and a huge ransom was demanded. Later, Chief Detective You A'gen of the Zhabei Police Station rescued Le from a villa at No. 911 Haige Road and arrested more than ten people, including Ma Gensheng, Guan Afu, and Ren Zixiang, who were handed over to the First Special Court for sentencing. However, according to the confessions of the criminals, the main culprit in this case was Lu Jinbao (also known as Yunlun Jiting), a Taizhou native and the owner of the Lulinji Automobile Company on Kunming Road. Because Lu was on the run at the time, the court issued an arrest warrant. Subsequently, Chief Detective You and Detective Liu Junqing arrested Lu on Edward Road and sent him to the First Special Court. Because the case files of Ma Gensheng and others had been sent to the Supreme Court, it was difficult to proceed, and the court ordered a rescheduling. More than four months have passed since then, and the files have now been returned. Yesterday, Judge Feng Shide of the court's criminal division opened the trial. Lu Yunlun hired lawyer Zhan Jifeng for defense, and police lawyer Li Zhishan stated that the police had found that the defendant was also involved in the kidnapping cases of Sheng Yishao and Tian Wuxing, and therefore added charges. Le Zhenbao then submitted a petition detailing his kidnapping experience, stating that after being kidnapped, the bandits ordered him to sit facing the wall and put on dark glasses, so he did not see the faces of the bandits. The court asked if the defendant had been seen in the bandits' lair, and he replied that he had not. When questioned, Lu Yunlun resolutely denied the charges and said that he did not know any of the convicted criminals. Police lawyer Li stated that Liu Ziyu had been sentenced to death for kidnapping Fan Aisheng, but Liu was also an accomplice in the kidnappings of Le Zhenbao and Tian Wuxing. The police had originally intended to prosecute him together, but if they did so, the same case would have to be handled by two judges, which would be more troublesome, so it was included in this case to save time. However, Liu Ziyu was not present today, so he requested a rescheduling. Judge Feng ordered a rescheduling for one week. Lawyer Zhan then stated that the defendant was currently detained in the West Prison on Huade Road, which was inconvenient for meeting and collecting evidence. Therefore, he requested that the defendant be temporarily detained at the police station, as his life was at stake, and asked the court to approve the request. The court approved the request.

The Japanese Consulate Prosecutes the Apple Box Smuggling Case: Cunning Merchant Cao Jianqiu Colludes with Japanese People in Fraud 143

According to yesterday's Japanese Shanghai Daily News, Osaka native Iuchi Hisayoshi, currently residing at No. 9, Tongqing Lane, Zhabei Road, came to Shanghai in 1932. In May of the same year, he established the Second Da Jinzi Company on Minhang Road, which was later renamed Da Haiyang Company. Last year, he returned to his country and met his fellow fruit merchant Kisamuro Hashimura, who asked him to come to Shanghai to sell Korean apples. In January of this year, Hashimura secretly mixed 1,700 pounds of rayon into 160 boxes of apples and shipped them from Incheon Port in Korea to the Shanghai Da Haiyang Company. He also entrusted Masataka Naramura from Okayama (currently residing at No. 6, Lane 44, Youheng Road) to sell them. Masataka then contacted Cao Jianqiu, a Chinese merchant at the Chengdang Ocean Company on Youheng Road, and a deal was reached. On February 2nd, he went to Higuchi Customs Brokerage to complete customs clearance procedures in the name of Chengdang Ocean Company. The goods had safely landed at the Yushan Wharf on Zhabei Road, but the matter was discovered by a warehouse manager, and the secret smuggling was not achieved. After interrogation by the Consul General, the whole story was clarified, and the two criminals will be prosecuted.

A Soldier Beaten and Injured: A Car Collision Led to Negotiations, and the Soldier Was Struck on the Head, Bleeding, and Sent to the Hospital for Treatment 144

At about 1:10 PM yesterday afternoon, at the corner of the intersection of Kaisen Road and Dunxin Road in Shanghai West, a truck with city license number 3392, driven by Lu Baolin, was speeding from east to west. When turning, he accidentally collided with a private car with city license number 6418, driven by an American, causing damage to the front of the car. As the two sides were stopping to negotiate, a police car dispatched from the Jingansi Police Station with officers number 256 (a Western officer) and number 332 (a Chinese officer) arrived. The Western officer went forward to investigate. By this time, a crowd had gathered. Suddenly, two soldiers from the security team stationed at the nearby Sanjing Temple, Chen Genrong and Dai Jinwen, caught sight of the crowd and went forward to watch. However, as soon as they arrived, the Western officer, for some unknown reason, kicked soldier Chen Genrong violently. Chen tried to endure the pain and ask questions, but Dai Jinwen felt that the Western officer's actions were unreasonable, as the two sides could not communicate. He immediately pulled Chen away by the arms, trying to bear the pain and leave. Unexpectedly, after only a few steps, the Western officer turned around and caught up, pulled out a baton from his waist, and struck Chen on the top of his head, causing him to bleed and fall to the ground in pain. Dai then returned to the team to report. The Western officer, seeing that he had caused trouble, immediately got into the car and sped away. The police officer on duty at the Kaisen Road observation post in District Six heard about it and rushed to the scene to investigate. He immediately reported to District Six, which in turn reported to the General Bureau for verification. The injured soldier was also taken to the Red Cross Hospital for treatment.

Shao Yunpeng, Yunfa, Yunjun, Yunqi, Yunlin, and Yunxiang, natives of Yuyao and nephews of the late Sheng Xuanhuai, filed a criminal lawsuit and attached civil suit against Sheng's brothers, sisters, nephews, and nieces last year after their maternal grandmother, Sheng Zhuangshi, passed away and her estate was divided by her descendants. They claimed that their mother should also have received a share, but it was seized by their maternal uncle, Sheng Zecheng, and others. According to the plaintiffs' lawyer, the amount of Sheng Zhuangshi's estate needs to be determined by reviewing the previous criminal case files. Therefore, the amount of litigation fees to be paid must be determined after the amount is verified. Judge Qiao then ordered a rescheduling for further verification.

After Hu Ganqing's Death, an Outside Wife Sues for Division of Property: Repeated Settlements Fail, Arguments Concluded, and Judgment Scheduled 146

Hu Ganqing, a native of Hangzhou and a shareholder in Fuchang Ginseng Shop in Nanshi and Hu Qingyutang Pharmacy on Beijing Road, left a considerable estate after his death the year before last. In addition to his shares in the two shops, he also owned a residence on Guling Road, worth more than 100,000 yuan. He also had a penchant for women and had three concubines, one surnamed Xue and two surnamed Li. Recently, Xue, accompanied by her daughter Hu Qiaoyun, hired lawyer Lu Dingkui to file a lawsuit with the civil court of the First Special District Court against Hu Shanqing, Hu Ganqing's son, requesting a division of one-third of the 300,000 yuan estate. The court has repeatedly opened trials, ordering the parties to try to settle out of court. The details have been reported in this newspaper. Yesterday afternoon, Judge Shen Hong again took the bench in Civil Division Six to continue the trial and asked both parties about the settlement situation. According to the defendant's lawyers, Lu Shaozong and Lin Yinqing, since the case was rescheduled, the two parties had once tried to settle, and the defendant was willing to pay 3,000 yuan and a monthly allowance of 30 yuan to the plaintiff, but the plaintiff thought it was too far off and refused to settle. Then, the plaintiff's lawyer, Lu Dingkui, stated that it was not that the plaintiff refused to settle. The defendant owns a huge amount of property, such as a residence on Guling Road, worth 140,000 yuan, plus shares in various places, totaling several hundred thousand yuan. Now the defendant is only willing to pay 3,000 yuan and 30 yuan per month, which is too small to settle. Moreover, the current assets of the Fuchang Ginseng Shop are estimated to be over a million, and Hu Ganqing alone accounts for five shares. According to the shop's books, the dividends under Hu Ganqing's name reach as high as 10,000 taels each year. Therefore, the amount requested by the plaintiff is not beyond the defendant's ability to pay. He requested that the court order the defendant to allocate one-third of the property to Qiaoyun and 14,580 yuan for the plaintiff's living expenses. Judge Shen then asked the defendant Hu Shanqing if he could increase the amount to the plaintiff. Hu replied that he could not, because his late father still had two concubines surnamed Li at home. If he increased the amount again, the two concubines at home would definitely request the same. Then, Madam Hu Xue stated that since her husband's death, her family has been paying her a monthly living allowance of 30 yuan, but it was suddenly stopped on the second day of the first month of this year. She now requests that the trial proceed. Judge Shen, considering the case clear, ordered the arguments to begin. The lawyers for both parties then argued for a long time. The court adjourned the arguments and scheduled the judgment for 2:00 PM on April 19.

Taikang Company's New Factory Opens Yesterday 149

The main store of Taikang Company on Nanjing Road opened on March 31st, with great success. Yesterday, it held an opening ceremony for its new factory, located on the bank of Nanfenglin Bridge. From 8:00 AM to 6:00 PM, guests gathered at the Nanjing Road main store and were transported to the factory in group buses. No less than three or four thousand guests attended. Upon leaving the factory, each person received a large bag of biscuits and candies with a voucher, and everyone who received it was happy. The details of the opening ceremony are as follows:

General Layout: The factory gate faces Xiaomubiao Road, and the 150

buildings face south, with bright light and ample air. A colorful archway is erected at the front gate, decorated with the words "Opening Ceremony" and "Welcome." Tea and refreshments, made by the factory, are served in the reception hall and upstairs, which are exquisite and fresh. The walls are filled with inscriptions and gifts, a feast for the eyes. The inscriptions of celebrities such as Chiang Kai-shek, Chen Gongbo, Wang Xiaolai, Du Yuesheng, and Yu Qiaqing add to the splendor. Visitors are led by the reception, and the entrance and exit are clearly marked. Although there are many guests, the order is well-maintained.

Key Equipment: The factory building is divided into three main sections. The back section, at the entrance, has several rooms for offices, as well as raw material storage, mouth-point manufacturing department, Western-style pastry manufacturing department, bread manufacturing department, canned food seasoning department, utensil storage room, welding department, restaurant, and after-work night school. The middle section has the machine room and woodworking department at the back, and the canned food manufacturing department, machine can-making department, canning and weighing sealing cooling department, and biscuit manufacturing department downstairs in the middle section. Upstairs are the flour sifting room and packaging room. Among them, the machinery for biscuit manufacturing is the most convenient and efficient in terms of layout and sequence, and the daily output is over 100,000. This is because the machinery is newly purchased and is the best in China. The front section is the dormitory and warehouse, and there is another room that is a chemical research laboratory, with equipment such as a constant temperature device and a fat measuring device for testing canned goods. The equipment can be described as complete.

Ceremony Report: There is a hall upstairs in the reception hall, with a table in the middle covered with a red curtain. At 10:30 AM, the meeting began with music, and the distinguished guests gathered. After performing the ceremony as usual, Ye Yunzhi, the chairman of the factory's board of directors, delivered a speech. Guest Yue Junbao performed the unveiling ceremony, and at the same time, cannons were fired and flags were raised. Then, General Manager Yue Rucheng reported on the evolution of the business, followed by speeches by Fang Jiaobo, Zhang Shenzhi, Wu Yaqin, and Hong Yanbin. The speeches were mostly praises and encouragements, which are omitted due to length. After that, the chairman gave a thank you, took photos, and served tea and refreshments. The ceremony was completed and the meeting adjourned.

Excerpt from the Evolution: Taikang was founded in Jinan in 1914 by Yue Rucheng, Xu Yongchun, and Zhuang Baokang. It was initially an unlimited partnership that sold Chinese and foreign foods. It then imitated the production of canned foods, candies, and biscuits. It expanded several times in 1918, 1921, 1922, and 1923. In the winter of 1921, it first established a wholesale office in Shanghai. In 1927, it changed from an unlimited company to a limited company with a paid-up capital of 150,000 yuan and was approved for registration. In 1933, it again increased its capital to 500,000 yuan. Today, its products are sold all over the country, and even to Little Luzon, Rangoon, Singapore, and Siam. Its five-pound "Fu" character red tin biscuits and spiced ribbonfish, whose quality is superior to imported products and have a special flavor, are especially well-known in the world.

Fish Industry Guild Answers Regarding British-Produced Small Green Kawakawa Fish: Can Verify if Markings Match 151

The Shanghai National Goods Factories United Association received a letter from the Dinghai Anti-Japanese National Salvation Association stating that upon investigation, some small Green Kawakawa fish have certificates from the Canadian or American consulate, and fish merchants in the county are requesting to sell them. Some have no certificates, and even those with certificates have discrepancies in the quantity of goods arriving, either exceeding or falling short of what is stated on the certificate (e.g., the certificate states five boxes, but there are only two boxes, or one box, or seven boxes of Green Kawakawa fish). The question is whether these Green Kawakawa fish without certificates or with discrepancies are enemy goods, and a request was made for investigation. After receiving the letter, the association sent a letter to the Shanghai Salted Fish Industry Guild for inquiry. Yesterday, the guild replied, stating that the small Green Kawakawa fish are produced in British Canada and are handled by German, American, British, and Japanese merchants. They are not produced in Taiwan. The goods sold by the guild's members are purchased from German and British merchants. The discrepancy in the number of boxes and the certificate is due to the certificate being pre-printed. For example, if the certificate is printed for five boxes, but the purchaser only buys two boxes, they can only attach the five-box certificate. The box markings can be compared with the certificate markings to see if they match. If they do not match, they are enemy goods. Some unscrupulous merchants do sell enemy goods, and their box markings are inconsistent, meaning the goods lack proper certification.

China-America Tobacco Company Initiates Four Principles for Promoting Domestic Cigarettes: Guanghua Brand Cigarettes Realize These Principles, Entitled the True Meaning of Chinese Standard Cigarettes 152

The China-America Tobacco Company, established for less than a year, has seen its Red and Blue "Buy Sigan" brand cigarettes become popular nationwide, making it a rising authority in the Chinese tobacco industry. The company's staff is further encouraged to establish unwavering principles in the movement to promote domestic cigarettes, serving as pioneers in changing the previous imitation of foreign styles. The Guanghua brand cigarettes, launched yesterday, were produced to realize these principles. The so-called principles are fourfold: 1) the flavor of the cigarettes must be richer than foreign cigarettes; 2) the price must be lower than foreign cigarettes; 3) the quality must be guaranteed never to change; 4) the packaging must have a spirit of innovation. The Guanghua brand's packaging uses ancient cultural relics for the can design, with elegant colors and purely Eastern art, with few foreign words. This alone is an unprecedented creation in the Chinese cigarette industry. Moreover, the flavor is rich, the price is low, and the quality is guaranteed to remain unchanged. Entitled "Chinese Standard Cigarettes," who would say it is not appropriate? They are sold at Wing On, Sincere, The Sun Sun, Lihua, The China National Goods Company, Fuan, and major tobacco and paper shops throughout the city, priced at four jiao per pack.

Hu Die Sues South China Society for Termination of Trademark Contract; Debate Concluded, Sentence Scheduled 159

The South China Chemical Industry Society previously signed a contract with movie queen Hu Die, using her portrait as a trademark to manufacture various cosmetics such as toothpaste, cologne, powder, and vanishing cream. At the time of signing the contract, 1,000 yuan in cash was paid, and a percentage of the annual operating income would be sent to Hu Die as compensation. However, the contract included a note stating that if, after one year of signing the contract, South China Society did not manufacture and sell the goods, Hu Die could request termination of the contract at any time. Subsequently, South China Society engaged in manufacturing goods and advertising their release, which caused a dispute with the Invincible Brand trademark of the Family Industry Society, leading to years of litigation. South China Society delayed manufacturing and selling goods due to the litigation. Hu Die believed that South China Society violated the contract and requested South China Society to terminate the contract, which was rejected. Therefore, she hired a lawyer to file a lawsuit in the Second Special District Local Court, requesting termination of the contract with South China Society. However, the initial trial resulted in Hu Die's failure. Hu Die then hired lawyers Feng Xizui and Qin Liankui to appeal to the Third Branch of the Jiangsu High Court. After the High Court opened an investigation court to review the evidence and concluded, the case was heard the day before yesterday by presiding judge Guo Dezhang, along with associate judges Zhang Chaozuo and Li Shouyi. Both parties were represented by lawyers. The court first summoned a person A, the director of Bao Wen Printing Press, to testify about the process of printing the silver star toothpaste, powder, and Hu Die toothpaste envelopes for the South China Chemical Industry Society, and verified the samples of the three envelopes submitted and the account books. Subsequently, after the appellant's lawyers Feng and Qin and the appellee's lawyers Zhang Shizhao and Peng Zhouxun debated, the court ordered the conclusion of the debate and announced that a sentence would be scheduled.

It was also decided that the situation discussed today should be reported to the three chairmen Xu, Du, and Zhang for approval. It was unanimously said that the three chairmen were very concerned about the hospital and would surely take good care of it in the future. It was then discussed that future donation receipts should be signed and sealed jointly by the president and the finance director to show solemnity. Everyone agreed and passed it unanimously. The meeting was then adjourned after dinner.

After Separation, Lawsuit Filed Over Son's Education 164

In the Wanzhao Courtyard, Fuxiang Lane, Fuzhou Road, there was a prostitute named Zhou Laoqi, who was favored by the customer Huang Jianqing. In January of the year before last, the two began living together in a room downstairs in Wanzhao Building. The prostitute soon became pregnant, and in September of that year, she gave birth to a son, named Shouhua, who is now three years old. However, Huang Jianqing, although fond of sensuality, was not devoted. Last year, he wanted to abandon Zhou, and a lawsuit was filed in the Second Special District Local Court. The court ruled to allow the separation of the couple, and ordered Huang Jianqing to pay Zhou Laoqi 3,000 yuan in alimony. Now, Zhou claims that Huang has a responsibility to raise and educate the son he had with her, but Huang has long stopped providing living expenses. If she does not negotiate with him, the child will inevitably suffer from cold and hunger. Therefore, as the legal guardian, she hired a lawyer to file a lawsuit against Huang in the First Special District Local Court, requesting: 1) confirmation that Huang Shouhua is Huang Jianqing's biological son; 2) an order for Huang Jianqing to pay 8,000 yuan in one lump sum to be deposited in a bank with 5% interest, which would yield 40 yuan per month for Huang Shouhua's living expenses; 3) an order for Huang Jianqing to pay 4,000 yuan for Huang Shouhua's education from elementary school to university graduation. The First Special District Court has already summoned him, and due to the need to summon additional witnesses, the hearing was postponed to yesterday afternoon. The witness Zhong Shuzhen, a female obstetrician, testified that she went to Zhou Laoqi's house to deliver the baby when Zhou was in labor, and at that time Zhou was living in Sandefang. Fang Xiuying, a woman, testified that she was Zhou Laoqi's cousin, Laoqi was Huang Jianqing's concubine, and Shouhua was born to Jianqing and Laoqi. She also went to the banquet in Sandefang when the child was one month old, and there were five or six tables of guests that day. Subsequently, the debate began. The plaintiff's lawyer said that there was considerable evidence regarding the biological son issue, and the defendant should be responsible for education. According to the law, the child can be taken away by the father, but the defendant has already separated from Zhou, and the defendant has not provided alimony since last year. When the case was filed in the Second Special District Court, the defendant even denied paternity, so he has no affection for his son and cannot be expected to educate him. Now that there are these special circumstances, the child is only three years old and still needs breastfeeding. It is impossible to separate the mother and child. Therefore, they requested that the child be allowed to be raised by his mother and that the defendant be ordered to provide living and education expenses totaling 12,000 yuan. Furthermore, the defendant is about to go to Japan, and to avoid difficulties in enforcement, they requested that the defendant be ordered to pay the amount in one lump sum. The defendant's lawyer replied that Zhou Laoqi was still living a dissolute life when she was pregnant, so according to the law, he cannot be recognized as the biological father and can only be considered an adopted son. Now that Zhou has separated from the defendant, the defendant should raise him, so there is no question of living and education expenses at all. They requested that the original lawsuit be rejected. Judge Qiao then ordered that a sentence be scheduled.

The meeting adjourned after the discussion.

Measures to Ban Pirated Books in the Book Industry 167

The Shanghai Book Industry Association has newly established ten measures to ban pirated books, which have been notified to all members and binding and printing bureaus for compliance. The measures are listed below: Article 1: The association has specifically established measures to ban pirated books in order to protect copyrights and avoid losses to members. Article 2: The association should write to the Shanghai Printing Industry Association to forward the following points to the printing industry for attention: 1) All printed books should be handled in accordance with the provisions of Article 16 of the Publication Law. If the book does not indicate the publisher's address, name, date of publication, and store number, and there is no formal letter of authorization, it shall not be printed. 2) It is necessary to verify the accuracy of the publisher's name, address, and store number mentioned above to prevent counterfeiting. Otherwise, the printing press that undertakes the printing will be responsible. 3) The printing press that undertakes the printing of books must comply with the Publication Law and print the address and store number of the store at the end to clarify responsibility. Article 3: The association will notify all binding shops that if a book does not indicate the publisher's accurate name, address, and store number, and does not have a formal letter of authorization, it shall not be bound. Otherwise, if pirating occurs, the binding shop shall be responsible. However, this does not apply to repairing old books. Article 4: All booksellers who publish books should submit the manuscript to the Ministry of the Interior for permission in accordance with the regulations of the Publication Law Implementation Rules. After approval, publish a notice in the newspaper to protect their rights. Article 5: All booksellers must not sell pirated books. Article 6: When selling original books, no matter how many, they should obtain a formal invoice or receipt from the original publishing headquarters, branch, and reseller as proof. Article 7: If an individual entrusts a member of the industry to consign books for sale, the consignee should clearly know the real name and address of the consignor before selling them. Otherwise, if it is a pirated book, the consignee will be responsible. Article 8: If books are sent from other places and entrusted to a member of the industry for sale, it is necessary to verify whether they are pirated books. If it is not easy to identify, they should be submitted to the association for public review. Article 9: When selling old books, members of the industry must not buy pirated books. If there is a book that is not easy to identify, they should inquire about and prove it to the industry association, the original publisher, or the reseller. Otherwise, once discovered, the member who purchased it will be responsible. Article 10: If a member of the association or a business partner is privately engaged in pirating, once the association's investigation is confirmed, it will be handled according to law.
