Discussion on the Marriageable Age 255

— Ji Jilin

Marriage is the most important and essential stage in the process of human life; no one can deny this, except for those who advocate religious asceticism.

The maintenance of human life depends on the reproduction of both sexes, and marriage is the way to achieve reproduction. Therefore, marriage is not only a personal matter but also an important task in human development. If we do not study everything about marriage and marry blindly, the result will inevitably affect the future of human development. Many scholars recognize marriage as a human obligation, and they also use a human perspective to argue this.

The Chinese people, oppressed under a patriarchal society, have been poisoned by the hypocrisy of the old rituals and attach importance to impractical procedures such as "parents' arrangement, six rites accompanying" for the marriage of the two sexes. As for the development of the two sexes and whether or not the marriageable age is appropriate, they have never taken it into consideration. The parents of both sexes have little education and more ignorance. They are dominated by the ancient teachings of "men must marry when they are old, women must marry when they are old" and the medieval concept of carrying on the family line. They want to taste the joy of having grandchildren and quickly complete the marriage of their children to fulfill their life's wishes. As a result, some people find happiness through marriage, while others enter a pessimistic path.

When humans reach the age of fourteen, although there are also those who reach it as early as twelve and as late as seventeen, special changes occur in their bodies. This change is a symbol of the maturity of both sexes, which medicine calls the period of puberty. When males reach this period, their voices become rough and turbid, their appearance tends to be beautified, their bones and flesh become more solid and strong, their bodies develop into beautiful and full forms, and hair grows on the lips, armpits, and other parts, especially the reproductive organs undergo significant changes. The seed of human reproduction, semen, begins to be secreted at this time. When females reach this period, the changes in their bodies are even more significant than those in males: the muscles become plump, the skin becomes smooth, and the beauty of female youth is fully manifested. The breasts and all of the reproductive organs are unusually developed. At the same time, menstruation begins. During puberty, not only do physical changes occur in both sexes, but there are also characteristic changes in the mental aspect. In particular, they know the need for sex, and there is now a clear understanding of the previously vague distinction between the two sexes.

Since the need for sex begins during puberty, the earliness or lateness of puberty is closely related to the age of marriage. Therefore, the marriageable age of people in various countries around the world is determined based on the earliness or lateness of puberty. Generally speaking, people in temperate zones have an earlier puberty and marry earlier. People in cold zones have a later puberty and marry later. In Germany, where medicine is most developed, the civil law stipulates that the marriageable age for males must be over twenty-five and for females over twenty-one. This is also determined based on the age of puberty. As for why women marry earlier than men, this is because women lose their sexuality earlier than men.

Many people advocate marriage at the beginning of puberty. Their reasons are:

(1) Sexual desire is a human instinct and is as important as appetite. It is actually harmless to marry when one knows the need for sex.

(2) Early marriage can eliminate harmful masturbation and nocturnal emission, resulting in a healthier sexuality.

(3) Early marriage can prevent immoral behavior and avoid the danger of venereal disease transmission.

These are indeed considerable reasons and cannot be absolutely denied. However, we should know that although sexual development is complete during puberty, the development of other parts of the body is still ongoing. If we only consider the completeness of sex and disregard other circumstances, we will definitely get the following results.

(1) It will affect the health and development of the body.

(2) Underage men and women have weak wills and cannot restrain excessive sexual desire.

(3) The children born are congenitally deficient and unhealthy, affecting the future of the race.

(4) They are too young and have insufficient knowledge to be role models for their children.

Moreover, according to biology, the marriage of the two sexes should take place after puberty. If they marry before reaching full age, they will inevitably fall into weakness and decline. Not only that, even from a social, economic, and intellectual point of view, early marriage never has good results. While we oppose early marriage, we do not approve of late marriage either, because each has equal harm. We advocate marriage at the appropriate age, preferably for males from twenty-five to thirty years old, and for females four to five years earlier than males. As for masturbation and venereal disease, these are indeed bad behaviors that are harmful to the body, but they can be remedied by sexual education. Parents who grew up under the old rituals think that sexual desire is a dirty and base behavior. This is a false concept. Mr. William Ludson of the United States advocates that children from the ages of ten to thirteen should be taught simple anatomy and physiology of the reproductive organs. From the ages of thirteen to sixteen, they can be explained the dangers of venereal diseases and the harmfulness of masturbation. As for everything that has a seductive instinct, lewd books, lewd pictures, and lewd plays should be strictly prohibited from contacting children. At the same time, try to arouse children's interest in studying and spend the elements that make up their sexual energy on the path of research. So that the instinct of sex can be naturally restrained and melted, this is indeed a good way. Unfortunately, education in our country has not been popularized, and there are many stubborn parents. Who can break the hypocrisy of the rituals and pay attention to sexual education?

A Simple Explanation of Pulmonary Tuberculosis (1) 256

— Hu Jiayan

Introduction

The disease of tuberculosis has been highly regarded in our country's traditional society! There is a popular saying among the common people, which goes: 'Paralysis, dropsy, and diaphragmatic obstruction are four incurable serious illnesses.' This saying has certainly been passed down from ancient times and contains considerable factual truth. However, we must understand that paralysis, dropsy, and diaphragmatic obstruction are only important symptoms within each disease, and not a disease in themselves. Examples of these types of symptoms occurring in each disease are numerous. Only the word 'consumption' (癆) is different from the others, ultimately representing the disease we call tuberculosis. In a narrow sense, it can also be called by another name, which is the pulmonary consumption (tuberculosis) mentioned in this topic. Looking back, what is the perspective of the modern medical community? They all commonly recognize that tuberculosis, syphilis, and cancer are the three major diseases worldwide. This view is entirely based on facts and is naturally much more insightful than the former. Regarding cancer, its causes and treatments have not yet been concretely determined, so we will leave it aside for now. Syphilis is different; its cause is completely understood, and there are specific drugs for treatment. However, if we observe from the perspective of transmission, the prevention of syphilis transmission is not entirely impossible. It is mostly caused by sexual intercourse with unclean individuals, and hereditary examples are also numerous. Therefore, if these two factors are absent, the risk of its transmission will be better in any case. Tuberculosis is completely different! Its only route of transmission, the reality of inhalation transmission, is difficult to prevent. We must understand that everyone's need for air is more common than 'food and sex'; it is even more important. In other words, one cannot survive without breathing air. Therefore, we can say that no one is not afraid of contracting tuberculosis. On the other hand, if we speculate about the future, modern material civilization is advancing without end. Industrial areas with dense populations and large cities with congested traffic are naturally becoming more and more numerous. However, this kind of development is very beneficial to the spread of tuberculosis. In other words, we can also say that the spread of tuberculosis will also advance without end. Syphilis is somewhat different in this situation because it has specific drugs as a backup, and industrial development is not directly related to it. Therefore, if we compare tuberculosis and syphilis as major enemies of humanity, 'equally outstanding talents' is not a problem. However, in terms of its 'pervasive' and 'advancing without end' transmission, the seat of the eldest brother will probably still have to be given to tuberculosis.

The fact that tuberculosis is a major enemy of humanity and its ease of transmission have already been mentioned somewhat above. So, is there any statistic on those who suffer from this disease? In China, there is no documentation. European scholars answer that those who die from this disease account for one-seventh of the total number of human deaths, but in prosperous cities or industrial areas, it is more than this number. This alarming number is more than any other disease. In Germany, previous reports indicated that no less than 100,000 people die from this disease each year, of which almost 90 percent suffer from pulmonary tuberculosis. In addition, calculated per 10,000 people, it is an average of about 17 percent in Germany, and 21 percent in Switzerland and France. Furthermore, observed by age, it can occur at any stage. Not to mention the prime of life in the twenties and thirties, there are already deaths from this disease among one- or two-year-old children, and the number of deaths is even greater among older people in their fifties and sixties. This fact can very well prove that the common saying in our country, 'People over forty years old do not contract tuberculosis,' is a misconception. Any of the above mortality figures we randomly pick are very shocking. No wonder the great German pathologist Ascboff exclaimed, 'No one is free from consumption,' a shocking statement.

A Brief Biography of Émile Roux, Director of the Pasteur Institute in France 257

Interpreted by Zhu Jiajian, Professor at the Sino-French University in Beiping

Today, doctors in various countries around the world all know to use serum therapy, which is fast and effective and can treat critical illnesses that other drugs cannot treat. For example, in the case of diphtheria, before the invention of serum, those who contracted it often faced the threat of death. Now, with serum treatment, they are safe and sound. It should be noted that the method of serum therapy, although now widespread around the world and saving countless lives, its invention is not far from the present. It is truly a great achievement of the modern medical community. And its inventor, the great French physician Émile Roux, passed away only three months ago. The French government buried him with state honors, which is not without reason. Now, I will briefly describe the person of Dr. Roux and his academic achievements as follows.

(1) Dr. Roux's Character and Exemplary Life 258

Dr. Roux was born on December 17, 1853, in Confolens, France. His father was the principal of a local middle school and died early, leaving behind nine children. Two sons died in the Franco-Prussian War. After graduating from middle school, Dr. Roux entered the medical department of the University of Clermont-Ferrand. Later, through the connection of his former chemistry professor, Mr. Dutilleux, he transferred to the University of Paris and became Mr. Dutilleux's assistant. In 1878, when the great physician Pasteur sought medical collaborators, Dr. Roux went to join him at Mr. Dutilleux's suggestion. Dr. Roux participated in all of Dr. Pasteur's research work. In 1883, Dr. Roux was sent by Dr. Pasteur to study Asian cholera. He returned to France the following year, and Dr. Pasteur immediately had him participate in the ongoing rabies research. Subsequently, in the years from 1885 to 1889, Dr. Roux announced his invention of anthrax and his research on infectious diseases of pigs. At the same time, starting in 1887, Dr. Roux collaborated with two other doctors to co-discover the toxins of diphtheria bacteria. This research was the main reason why diphtheria serum could be prepared six years later. Since then, the new method of serum therapy has appeared in the world and will continue to advance without end. In addition to the serum for treating diphtheria, Dr. Roux also collaborated with two or three doctors to produce serum for treating tetanus, plague, pneumonia, and other diseases. Thus, Pasteur's pioneering work was promoted and expanded by this talented man, and France's science was able to bestow its benefits upon the world. When Dr. Pasteur passed away in 1895, Mr. Dutilleux succeeded him as the director of the institute, and Dr. Roux assisted him. Later, when Director Dutilleux passed away in 1904, Dr. Roux succeeded him. He had already been elected as a member of the Academy of Medicine in 1895 and was elected as a member of the Academy of Sciences in 1899. Dr. Roux's honors and awards were elevated step by step until he received the highest level of the Legion of Honor in 1920. However, since 1900, Dr. Roux, due to overwork, needed rest and recuperation, so he was unwilling to participate in the various inventions that had made the Pasteur Institute shine brightly since he was thirty-three years old. However, Dr. Roux also fulfilled his duties of instruction and guidance, so his contribution to the assistance is still unforgettable. Moreover, Dr. Roux especially liked to maintain and encourage general researchers who did not aim at profit, such as the two great doctors Metchniket and Golemet, who were both able to achieve their goals thanks to Dr. Roux's efforts. The characteristic of Dr. Roux's character can be summed up in one sentence: he was modest and empty-minded. As for his integrity, it was almost like that of a monk, and his humility was especially admirable. When he invented the serum for treating diphtheria, French President Casimir Perier intended to personally present him with the Legion of Honor. However, Dr. Roux did not know in advance. When the president wanted to wear the medal for him, Dr. Roux ran away and exclaimed loudly, "I have done nothing meritorious. This thing should belong to Behring!" So the president had no choice but to forcefully grab his clothes and put it on him. Furthermore, Dr. Roux was simple by nature and did not care for adornment. One day, he went to see Baron Rothschild to discuss the funding problem of the institute. The gatekeeper, seeing that his clothes were old and worn, was unwilling to let him through. Only after three requests did he transmit the message. After the audience, the host sent him to the door and said to him, "If one million is not enough, please tell me." Then the gatekeeper was greatly surprised. But we should not judge Dr. Roux as a cold-blooded person based on the above trivial matters. For example, Dr. Roux and Dr. Pasteur were extremely close, but they often expressed different theories to their teacher due to academic reasons, and even each insisted on their own views and refused to yield. However, when they met in the laboratory the next day, they were still as friendly as ever. Sometimes Dr. Roux's views were not wrong, and once they were confirmed, Dr. Pasteur also frankly admitted them.

The two major characteristics of Dr. Roux's nature, namely simplicity and perseverance, have already been expressed. Now, we must add a third characteristic to complete Dr. Roux's personality. This third characteristic is compassion. Although Dr. Roux remained unmarried throughout his life, he loved family life very much, so he maintained constant contact with his relatives. He was also exceptionally amiable to his collaborators, so everyone was happy to associate with him. Moreover, Dr. Roux's painstaking research on diphtheria was also motivated by his compassionate feelings, not for profit. So, wasn't Dr. Roux's ability to invent the unprecedented new method of serum therapy aided by his compassionate spirit of saving all living beings? The progress of French medicine in the past forty years is due to Dr. Roux's contribution.

(2) Dr. Roux's Scholarship and Character 259

Dr. Roux paid great attention to various physiological issues and also devoted himself to the study of various diseases. Therefore, the collaborators in the Pasteur Institute have mostly been influenced by Dr. Roux for thirty years. Even foreign specialized bacteriologists can all be called Dr. Roux's disciples. Dr. Roux established a bacteriology lecture hall on Dulot Street in 1889. At that time, more than 3,000 people came to listen, most of whom were foreign scholars and young doctors. Although Dr. Roux has passed away, his academic achievements have spread throughout the world, so Dr. Roux's spirit can be said to be immortal.

However, from the perspective of the general public, Dr. Roux is the person who invented the serum for treating diphtheria. Therefore, Dr. Roux is also the creator of serum therapy.

(3) Serum Therapy 260

The great physician Pasteur was a discoverer of the microbial world and had declared war on molds, destroying some of their strong points. Then he passed on his academic achievements to his disciples. His disciples then attacked the molds again, and the most powerful among them was undoubtedly the great physician Émile Roux. In 1887, Dr. Roux published an article in the weekly journal of the Pasteur Institute, detailing the method of using a solution obtained from molds for immunization. At that time, the great physician Pasteur immediately realized the importance of this invention. Therefore, he made a declaration at a general meeting in the Academy of Sciences, saying that he had now proven that a dangerous disease that causes rapid death (diphtheria) can be immunized by injecting a chemical quantity of matter. This substance comes from the life of microorganisms that can cause death.

The following year (1888), Dr. Roux and Mr. Yersin collaborated to discover the toxin in the culture juice of diphtheria bacteria. Later, in 1890, two doctors, Behring and Kitasato, proved in Germany that by injecting the toxin invented by Dr. Roux and Mr. Yersin into animals using appropriate methods, their serum would have the ability to resist diphtheria. Serum is a part of the blood and is separated from it when the blood clots. Therefore, animals injected with the toxin of Dr. Roux and Mr. Yersin developed a reaction to the toxin, thus creating an antitoxin, which has the ability to resist diphtheria.

Four years later, in October 1894, Dr. Roux announced his recent achievements in collaboration with two doctors, Mr. Massi and Mr. Shahou, at the International Health Congress in Budapest. At that time, people all over the world were filled with respect and gratitude. Doctors, mold experts, and veterinarians from various countries all rushed to study the new method or to obtain serum. However, because this thing was extremely rare and could not be given in large quantities, after the promotion of a certain newspaper, a donation of one million was obtained, which was used to organize the large-scale production of serum for treatment and various preventive drugs transformed from the toxin invented by Dr. Roux (to be continued).

New Book Introductions 261

1. Published on the 1st and 16th of each month.

Is There Communication Between Wire and Wireless? 264

— Lü Bing

Further Cooperation

Once wrote an article for a certain magazine in the telecommunications field. At that time, the National Government had not been established for long, and there was much discussion about developing transportation. Some proposed creating wired and wireless communication networks, which would be very effective and detailed, but considering the needs and economy, merchants were concerned that it might not be in line with the national conditions. Therefore, the author advocated at the time that the establishment of communication networks should not be divided by the boundaries of wired and wireless: "Where wired telegraph cannot reach, use telephone; where wired telegraph and telephone cannot reach, use wireless telegraph and wireless telephone, and communicate with each other to create a telecommunications network that reaches all parts of the country."

Although wired and wireless have a one-word difference in their names, they also have different materials and machinery in practice, but they are both communication weapons, which is beyond doubt. In the past, during the warlord era, wired and wireless were clearly divided, each establishing its own portal. In name, they belonged to the same transportation department, but in reality, "wired" and "wireless" were not coordinated. In recent years, with unified authority, development has also become balanced. Now, reading the newspaper, it is reported that the Ministry of Communications has also promulgated further cooperation methods for wired and wireless from April 1st. Although the actual rotation steps must wait for careful consideration and proper handling, the principle of "wired" and "wireless" communicating with each other has been established. Therefore, telegram senders do not have to ask whether wired or wireless can reach it. Just hand it over to the telegraph bureau for allocation, allowing it to be "wired" or "wireless," or "wireless" or "wired," with speed as the main goal, so that there is nothing that cannot be reached. This is really a great convenience for public communication. The so-called creation of the whole country as a large telecommunications network, the cooperation of wired and wireless, can be called the first step of success.

In terms of telegram business, telegrams often increase when accidents occur in the country. At this time, if the transmission of wireless is busy, wired can be used to coordinate. Dredging the telegram business and allocating work is like doing everything in an orderly manner. The so-called line congestion and the so-called telegram delay can be reduced substantially. The four words "rapid transmission" will be more realistically expressed after "wired and wireless communication," making senders and recipients exceptionally satisfied.

In short, further cooperation between wired and wireless to achieve communication and improve efficiency in business is not lacking in other countries, and my country should follow suit. External measures, such as joint registration, have been announced, and internal implementation, through the Ministry of Communications' careful planning, can be realized in a short period of time.

The New Life Movement and the Telecommunications Field 265

— Zhen

The New Life Movement originated in Nanchang, and then continued in Beijing, Shanghai, Pinghan, and other places. In the past month, it has swept the country, starting from the inspection of personal clothing, food, housing, and transportation to strengthen the foundation of the national society. It cannot be said that it is not a fundamental strategy for national salvation. The definition of the New Life Movement has been explained by Chairman Chiang: "People's lives of clothing, food, housing, and transportation must conform to propriety, righteousness, integrity, and a sense of shame." Propriety, righteousness, integrity, and a sense of shame are the essential conditions for our spiritual life, and clothing, food, housing, and transportation are the essential conditions for our material life. The needs of clothing, food, housing, and transportation must conform to propriety, righteousness, integrity, and a sense of shame, so that material desires have no cover; the essence of propriety, righteousness, integrity, and a sense of shame must be expressed in clothing, food, housing, and transportation, so that integrity is not in vain. We serve in the telecommunications field, and we make a living here. Looking back and observing the future, we should strive for the New Life Movement. Now, I will list a few items to show a glimpse. What is said to the society is also to encourage ourselves with propriety, righteousness, integrity, and a sense of shame. Telecommunications is a state-owned enterprise. In the past, the responsible officials were mostly from the political world, and they inevitably carried a bit of officialdom. The staff in the bureau were full of prestige, and the general public had long regarded the telecommunications bureau as a government office. After the establishment of the Ministry of Communications of the National Government, it was determined that the telecommunications business should be commercialized. The telecommunications bureau is like a store, the staff is like a clerk, and the people who send and receive telegrams and calls are the customers who are warmly welcomed in the store. The clerks must be kind and humble to the customers and must not be arrogant and rude. The Ministry of Communications has repeatedly given earnest admonitions, and the bureau staff also abide by them, but in addition to self-encouragement, we still hope for more supervision from the society.

For sending telegrams, there is a distinction between ordinary and urgent, and there is a difference in the order of sending and receiving. If the telegram cannot be delivered due to business reasons, or the telegram is wrong, or the delivery is too late, the telecommunications bureau also has clauses for full or partial refunds. This has been clearly stipulated in the telegram business rules. Since the telecommunications bureau collects the telegram fee from the sender, it should bear the responsibility for fast and accurate transmission. Rights and obligations should not be confused. It is righteous and appropriate that the bureau staff do their best to serve the society. What they should abide by is also where righteousness lies.

The telecommunications authorities, because the price of telegrams in our country is quite high and cannot be used by the general public, and when the telecommunications economy is extremely difficult, they cannot reduce the price of telegrams as much as possible, putting the maintenance of the business at risk. Therefore, in the absence of any other way, they have stipulated various measures: (1) The name and address of the recipient within 15 characters will be counted as 5 characters for billing; (2) The urgent telegram fee will be doubled; (3) Postal transfer telegrams will be free of postage; (4) Road transfer telegrams will be free of over-the-line fees; (5) Public telegrams inquiring about the meaning of the words will be allowed free of charge; (6) Domestic social telegrams, whether inter-provincial or intra-provincial, will be uniformly 2 cents per Chinese character and 4 cents per foreign character. For several months, efforts have been made to work on the word "cheap" in order to arouse the public's interest in sending telegrams. As for the integrity and integrity of the responsible personnel of the telecommunications authorities, the Ministry pays special attention to this.

The Ministry of Communications is ashamed of the international communication being controlled, so it established an international radio station to remedy it; it is ashamed of the old and outdated telephone machines, so it purchased telegraph clearing machines, printing machines, and automatic telephone machines to reform them. In order to solicit opinions from all walks of life, business inspectors were set up; in order to avoid errors in telegram transmission, proofreaders were assigned. For other facilities in business and engineering, the authorities are always concerned that our country's telecommunications is ashamed of not being able to keep pace with Europe and the United States, and they are always concerned that our country's telecommunications is ashamed of not being able to be fully utilized by the people of the whole country. "Knowing shame and being brave," the various reforms of the telecommunications administration in recent years are not the effect of the authorities being brave enough to take responsibility.

The above is just a brief discussion on the expression of propriety, righteousness, integrity, and a sense of shame in the telecommunications field, based on what I can remember. It is not worthy of elegance, but at this time of repeated internal and external troubles, the telecommunications field has a sense of vigor, which is in line with the true meaning of the New Life Movement. As the Western proverb says, "Facts speak louder than words," so putting it forward is not intentionally promoting the telecommunications administration.

The Reasons for the Advancement of Automatic Telephones in Recent Years 266

— Li Shaomei

Why has automatic telephone technology made such significant progress in our country recently? This is a very interesting question. If we wish to explain the reasons, it is more appropriate to explore the motivation and background:

(A) The original equipment of telephone bureaus has become dilapidated. The lifespan of telephone switching equipment is usually no more than ten years. During the maintenance period, one should plan for the replacement of old equipment with new, or set aside savings. When equipment becomes unusable, new machines should be purchased. However, due to various reasons, bureaus often find it difficult to attend to this in practice, resulting in mechanical equipment being used beyond its lifespan, which naturally affects operations. A look at the statistics of obstacles in the 17th year of various bureaus makes this clear.

Bureau | Number of Line Obstacles | Number of Internal Equipment Obstacles | Number of User Equipment Obstacles

------- | ------------------------ | ---------------------------------------- | ----------------------------------------

Capital | 25014 | 13356 | 66181

Shanghai | 12141 | 43726 | 471

Wuhan | 29681 | 16238 | 20921

Qingdao | 6606 | 3321 | 3023

In order to perfect the service and to meet the needs of society, there is a trend to abandon manual switching and replace it with automatic telephones.

(B) Heavy telephone traffic: The current charging system in domestic telephone bureaus is mostly a monthly flat rate. With a flat rate, users have unlimited telephone usage; even a single household installation may be shared with several other households. Looking at the exchange statistics of the 17th year of various telephone bureaus, the volume of telephone traffic is heavier than in major British and American cities with large populations and developed enterprises.

Bureau | Number of Users | Average Number of Calls Per User Per Day

------- | --------------- | -----------------------------------------

Capital | 22912 | 3

Shanghai | 20271 | 9

Wuhan | 4510 | 20

Qingdao | 2634 | 16

Given the heavy telephone traffic in various bureaus as mentioned above, it goes without saying that users often experience difficulties such as "line busy" and "not connected." To thoroughly improve operations, automatic telephones are necessary. The measured service system is difficult to implement quickly in China, which is another reason.

(C) Difficulty in managing and training telephone operators:

In Europe and America, telephone companies have specialized schools to train switchboard operators. Looking at their detailed operating rules, switchboard operators cannot easily adhere to them without rigorous training. In China, the training period for telephone operators is largely based on the traditional "apprenticeship" system. Over time, bad habits inevitably develop, causing difficulties in management. The resulting response is to replace manual labor with machines, which is also a reason for the advancement of automatic telephones.

(D) Modernization of telephones: The term "automatic telephone" is novel. Today, construction projects invariably use it as a slogan to attract attention. For example, Wanxian, Sichuan, has only about a hundred subscribers. Purchasing a magneto switchboard would be very economical, but they adopted automatic telephones, based on the Chinese people's psychology of imitating fashion. This alone can explain the rest.

(E) Overproduction in foreign factories: Recently, the economies of European and American countries have declined. The output of various factories has already exceeded domestic demand, resulting in a severe problem of overproduction. These countries are trying to sell overseas, intending to use the Far East as an outlet. During this period of electrical reorganization in our country, they are competing to promote sales with all their might. Automatic telephones are a profitable business, and naturally one of the targets of foreign factories.

(F) Seeking confidentiality and speed of communication: When using manual telephones, operators must be involved in connecting the lines. Even if they are well-trained, misunderstandings can easily arise due to physiological variations and differences in language. Furthermore, users ultimately do not trust that operators can absolutely abide by the rules and not eavesdrop on conversations. For example, during the Wuhan government era, the bureau's equipment was still manual, while military and government agencies used automatic machines that were centralized. This was partly to ensure the confidentiality of conversations, and partly to allow for rapid communication during emergencies. Other places, such as the Ministry of Railways and the Shenyang Arsenal, adopted automatic telephones very early, based on the reasons mentioned above.

One Aspect of Postal and Telegraph Cooperation (Postal Transfer of Telegrams) — China Postal Telegraph Bureau 267

Three Recent Major Contributions of German Telecommunications 268

— Luo Jiemin

Recent researchers of telegraphy all believe that telegraphs should tend towards "telephonization." Although teleprinters are common in various European and American countries, telecommunications engineers still consider them to need improvement. In 1928, Germany had "Residence Telegraphy" installations, where subscribers could rent dedicated lines from the local telegraph headquarters and install automatic teleprinters in their homes or businesses to communicate directly with other subscribers with similar equipment. However, due to various reasons, only a few large companies used this type of machine. The scope was small and difficult to popularize. The German Postal and Telegraph Department, recognizing this, conducted several studies and made the following three major contributions:

(I) Expansion of Automatic Teleprinters: It is planned to utilize existing telephone underground cables between various cities for the exclusive use of those who have installed automatic teleprinters. These circuits will connect each subscriber to an "automatic telegraph exchange," which will then distribute the messages. The equipment used by each subscriber will be installed by the managing agency after inspection, and maintained by the subscriber themselves. Berlin and Hamburg have already conducted trials, and the following three types of fees are stipulated per household, per month, per kilometer of dedicated line (referring to the distance from the subscriber's residence to the exchange):

A. Station rental fee: 5 marks

B. Line rental fee: 5 marks

C. Communication fee: 0.10 marks per six minutes, with an additional one-third for every two minutes thereafter, and a one-third reduction from 5:00 PM to 8:00 AM the next morning.

The printing is fully automatic. Subscribers only need to dial the number on a dial (similar to an automatic telephone dial) in their room to connect to the teleprinter of the person they wish to communicate with. Since there are ample circuits, there is no need to wait. If the recipient is not in the room, the printed message can be received automatically without error. There is a small box next to the machine with two keys and a dial. When sending a message, first flip and press the "Service" key to connect the circuit, then dial the recipient's call number (dialing method is the same as automatic telephone). Once the last number rebounds, communication can begin. After finishing, flip the "Eod" key to immediately disconnect the circuit. There is also a special "Reply" key dedicated to verifying the call. If the sender wants to know if the connection is correct after dialing, they can flip this key, and the recipient's teleprinter will automatically print out the recipient's name and address, thus eliminating the drawback of misconnection. The same procedure can be used to send messages to other places, which can be sent free of charge to the local telegraph bureau.

(II) Alternating Use of Telephone and Telegraph: This type of circuit for alternating telephone and telegraph use is a simple alternating current type, which can be called "Single Vocal Frequency Telegraphy." The equipment used is as shown in the diagram.

If subscriber FI in the diagram wants to talk to subscriber through central telegraph bureau FA, the branch line keys U1, U1 are as shown in the diagram. To send a message and record the conversation, simply twist the branch line keys U1, U2, and both parties can communicate on teleprinters M1, M2. After finishing, hang up the phone and the circuit will be disconnected. When no one is receiving telegrams at night, a "Night Commutator" can be installed. When the recipient is away, twisting this key will automatically enable the teleprinter to receive telegrams. After stopping, the circuit can be automatically disconnected within 30 seconds. The communication fee for this service is the same as the telephone fee, so subscribers can freely send telegrams or make calls without restriction. The installation of this type of telegraph machine does not affect the telephone system in any way. Whether it can send telegraphs or transfer electricity to various places is still under study.

(III) Wireless Automatic Teleprinter: To facilitate the simultaneous and rapid transmission of financial, sports, and other news, Germany is installing a "SiemensHell Teleprinter" for wireless transmission. This machine is very cheap to purchase and easy to manage, and anyone can send and receive messages. When the central station sends a message, most stations can receive it simultaneously. The received telegram is in facsimile format, and is identical to the sender's. The characteristics of this type of telegram are that it is simple, safe, not limited by long or short waves, and free from air interference. Furthermore, no one can illegally eavesdrop or intercept the transmission.

A Few Words About Kite Flying 269

— Guan

Spring is sunny and bright, making it ideal for flying kites. Kite flying is an old Chinese pastime. Enjoying oneself at the right time is appropriate, so many prominent figures now advocate its promotion. Adults and children who enjoy kite flying are naturally all the more excited to hear such news.

However, according to newspaper reports, airlines are considering banning kite flying because it obstructs flight targets. This is a setback for kite flying. I am not familiar with aviation, so I will talk about power lines. It is common to see fragments and remnants of kites hanging on power lines in and around cities during the spring season. This is the result of kite flying by our friends who are enjoying themselves. It should be known that power lines continuously transmit electricity. These dangling fragments become conductive when it rains, interfering with communication. If a kite falls and gets caught on a power line, climbing up to retrieve it is even more dangerous due to the risk of electric shock. Therefore, I am using this space in the magazine to inform our friends who enjoy kite flying in a timely manner:

Fly kites in a way that allows you to retrieve them. Do not let them touch power lines!

Regarding Temporary Cancellation of Long-Distance Telephone Calls 270

— Reporter

The Long-Distance Telephone Business Regulations promulgated by the Ministry of Communications on June 2nd of last year have been officially implemented since March 1st of this year. Article 7, Section 2 stipulates that if the caller requests a temporary cancellation of the call, the regulation is the same as Section 1, requiring a charge of one-third of the call fee. Outsiders believe that charging one-third of the call fee even when the call has not been connected seems overly harsh. According to inquiries by this reporter, the Ministry of Communications established this article in consideration of the interests of users, not out of severity. A brief account is given below:

Article 31, Section 7, Paragraph 1 of the Telephone Regulations annexed to the International Telecommunications Convention revised in Madrid states, "Except for pre-arranged calls, in the event of any call where the calling or receiving party refuses to speak, the fee due shall be equal to the fee for a one-minute ordinary call made by the two machines during the charging period at the time of receipt of the refusal, with the minimum charge being fifty centimes." In other words, if the calling or receiving party refuses to speak, a minimum fee of fifty centimes should be charged. Article 1 of the Ministry of Communications' Long-Distance Telephone Business Regulations is based on this section. In fact, when the calling party requests a call, the calling bureau must register it and transmit it to the receiving bureau in turn, and then notify the receiving party to answer the call. This procedure is quite complicated. If the calling party requests a temporary cancellation of the call after the calling bureau has already notified the receiving bureau, or when the receiving bureau has already notified the receiving party, not only does the long-distance line suffer a time loss, but the receiving party also experiences unnecessary trouble. Therefore, this article was specially established to show a restriction. According to the regulations in the telegram rules, if the sender requests to cancel a telegram that has already been transmitted, the telegraph bureau will only refund the message fee for the untransmitted portion of the journey. This has the same meaning as this article.

Furthermore, from the perspective of the user's interests, newspapers in Beijing and Shanghai often register arbitrarily during the busiest times for news transmission, regardless of whether they have any news, rushing to be first. When they are eventually connected in turn, if the newspaper has nothing to report at that time, they often request cancellation. Such a situation ties up long-distance lines, which is a minor issue, but it delays the transmission of news from other newspapers, which has a major impact. Therefore, for the convenience of most newspapers, a handling fee must be charged for this type of cancellation, which is ultimately more beneficial than harmful to the user.

In summary, while a calling party's temporary request to cancel a call is rare, a separate article had to be added to the legislation to ensure thoroughness. When the new Beijing-Shanghai line is completed and communication is smooth, there will be no impact from excessive registrations, and there will be no need for temporary cancellation requests.

In the past, when one wanted to send a telegram or mail a letter, one had to run around, which was very inconvenient. Now that the post office and telegraph office are merged, people from all walks of life can go to the same place to send telegrams or mail letters, saving a lot of trouble!

The second type of movement is the merger of wired and wireless telegraphy. Wired and wireless telegraphy are really just different forms of telegraph transmission with equivalent effects. They each have their strengths and weaknesses. If the two are merged and operated together, using each other's strengths, then the shortcomings of either wired or wireless telegraphy can be overcome, and the telegrams sent by the public can safely and quickly reach their destinations. In order to ensure the safety and speed of telegrams sent by the public, the Ministry of Communications resolutely ordered the merger of wired and wireless telegraphy management from April 1st. From now on, when sending telegrams, people simply need not specify whether to use "wired" or "wireless." Deciding on the transmission method can be entrusted to the bureau staff, as they can choose the most appropriate method based on various operational and technical factors.

The above two movements are general and apply to the whole country. In the Shanghai area, there is another cooperative movement, which is to combine all telegram registrations at the International Radio Station in Sassoon House on Nanjing Road, the Shanghai Telegraph Bureau at 7 Luchi Road, the National Wireless Radio Headquarters on Minguo Road, and the Great Northern Water Line Telegraph Office at 34 Edward Road, the Great Eastern Water Line Telegraph Office, and the Pacific Water Line Telegraph Office, under the newly established "Shanghai United Telegram Registration Office." This movement may seem small in scope, but it is also very significant. In the past, the telegram registrations at the above locations were not unified due to various reasons, such as the differences between wired and wireless telegraphy, the distinction between international and domestic telegrams, and the different positions of foreign underwater cable companies. As a result, some charged registration fees, some were free, and some had several registrants using the same registration word. The methods varied! Disputes arose from time to time, causing inconvenience to those sending telegrams. Now, telegram registrations at all locations have been unified! As long as business firms pay a registration fee at the "Shanghai United Telegram Registration Office," they can use it for telegrams transmitted by wired, wireless, and various submarine cables. Unifying the procedures and eliminating disputes is a great convenience for people sending telegrams in Shanghai.

The World of Telecommunications 271

— Zhen

(The Development of Automatic Telephones in Germany)

The German Postal and Telegraph Department's revitalization plan, with the government's economic assistance, will convert 200 manual telephone exchanges to automatic exchanges between New Year's Day and the end of March this year. Among them, 125 exchanges will use 100 trunk lines, 85 exchanges will use 200 trunk lines, 80 exchanges will use 1,000 trunk lines, and the remaining 10 exchanges will have more than 1,000 lines. As of New Year's Day this year, Germany has 5,445 exchanges, of which 2,228 are automatic. Work is continuing to convert all exchanges to automatic. (Report from the U.S. Commercial Attaché in Berlin)

(The Rise of Radio in Soviet Russia)

The Soviet Russian government has allocated £2 million this year to promote radio. Last year, Soviet Russia had 2 million radios, and this year it plans to install 950,000 new radios. Of these, 10% will be installed in rural areas.

(London Electrical Review)

(Improvement of Telegraph and Telephone Services in Austria)

The Austrian special budget for 1934 allocated 2.6 million schillings (one schilling equals 14 U.S. cents) for new installations by the Postal and Telegraph General Bureau. The business community is busy manufacturing large quantities of telegraph and telephone equipment. Last year, there was no long-distance telephone underground cable installed, but the government has allocated 7 million schillings for the installation of a submarine cable between Vienna and Pasace. (Report from the U.S. Consul General in Austria)

(Reduction of Telephone Rates in Australia)

The plan to promote rural automatic telephones has been announced by the Postmaster General, who hopes to establish 30 locations this year. He also proposed reducing the current telephone rate of £5 10s per household by £1. If business does not increase, this price reduction will result in an annual loss of approximately £35,000, but he believes that once the rate is reduced, users will be happy to use it. (Report from the U.S. Commercial Attaché in Ceylon)

(Opening of Facsimile Telegrams Between France and Italy)

Facsimile telegrams between Paris and Rome have been opened. The cost is based on the size of the area of the telegram, calculated at 1.85 francs per square centimeter, with a minimum cost of 185 francs. All French post offices accept this type of telegram. (London Electrical Review)

(Abolition of Morse Machines in the United Kingdom)

The British Post Office's plan to abolish Morse machines is in its final stages. By the end of the European War, the Morse machines on all main lines had been replaced with Baudot machines. For bureaus with a daily average of less than 70 telegrams, the voice transmission system is gradually being adopted. According to a report from the U.S. Commercial Attaché, this work has been implemented in various bureaus since 1929. Since then, domestic telegraph business has taken on a new look! The percentage of telegrams handled by each machine in 1929, 1932, and 1933 is listed below:

| Machine | 1929 | 1932 | 1933 |

|-------------|---------|---------|---------|

| Teleprinter | 16.1 | 69.5 | 72.3 |

| Voice Trans. | 13.5 | 15.0 | 21.3 |

| Morse | 28.4 | 9.0 | 3.5 |

| Multiplex | 37.7 | 4.6 | 1.3 |

| Other | 4.3 | 1.9 | 1.6 |

Once the new telegraph and telephone machines in the central telegraph bureau are in operation this year, the amount of Morse telegraph business listed in the right table will definitely be replaced by telephones. (London Telegraph and Telephone Monthly)

Semi-Monthly News 272

— Staff Member

(Commercial Dedicated Lines for Sending and Receiving Telegrams)

In major cities of various countries, telegraph bureaus and commercial firms that send many telegrams have special dedicated lines for sending and receiving telegrams in order to reduce delays in delivery by messengers, making communication very convenient for businesses. In order to expedite the sending and receiving of telegrams by commercial firms and mines in various locations, the Ministry of Communications has specially formulated the "Regulations for Commercial Dedicated Lines for Sending and Receiving Telegrams," which will be implemented from the date of promulgation of the regulations on March 31. The main points of the regulations are excerpted below:

1. Commercial dedicated lines are divided into telephone dedicated lines and telegraph machine dedicated lines. Those who wish to install them can contact the local telegraph bureau or station.

2. Those in areas with city telephone service can rent a dedicated line from the telephone bureau. Those without city telephone service can have the bureau or station install a dedicated line on their behalf. The line rental fee or installation fee shall be paid by the applicant.

3. Those installing telephone dedicated lines shall be responsible for the installation and rental fees of the telephones used at both ends. If it is necessary to rent a soundproof room at the bureau or station to install a telephone, a monthly rental fee of five yuan shall be paid. Otherwise, it is also possible not to rent.

4. Those installing telegraph machine dedicated lines shall have the required telegraph machines at both ends prepared by the bureau or station. The applicant can rent them from the bureau or station. If renting a teleprinter, a machine deposit of 2,000 yuan shall be paid, with a monthly rental fee of 40 yuan and an installation fee of 10 yuan. If renting a Morse machine, a machine deposit of 500 yuan shall be paid, with a monthly rental fee of 20 yuan and an installation fee of 10 yuan. The applicant shall be responsible for the salaries of the operators required at the applicant's end, but can borrow them from the bureau or station.

(Reduction of Domestic Social Telegram Prices)

Since its establishment by the Ministry of Communications, the domestic social telegram service has been praised by the public for its extremely low prices. However, the original pricing doubled the cost for telegrams sent to provinces other than the sender's province. As a result, domestic social telegrams between provinces were not very developed. In order to thoroughly benefit the people, the Ministry of Communications has now uniformly changed the pricing to be the same as that for telegrams within the same province, which is 2 cents per Chinese character and 4 cents per English character, effective from May 1st.

— Ji Qing

The aim is none other than to provide convenience to the general public

In the atmosphere of the enthusiastic promotion of the New Life Movement, the Ministry of Communications has recently undertaken several extremely important cooperative movements. Economic Supplement Published Every Monday Issue 68

The Situation of Global Cotton Industry Statistics 274

— Chu Yu

According to the statistics on the global cotton industry from the International Federation of Cotton Spinners' Associations for the first half of 1933-34 (i.e., from August 1 of last year to the end of January this year), the survey results show that the global consumption of cotton increased by 190,000 bales from February to July of last year. Among them, the consumption of Indian cotton and Egyptian cotton was the highest, while the consumption of American cotton decreased by 300,000 bales. If we look at the cotton consumption of each country separately, Germany increased by 114,000 bales, the United Kingdom increased by 104,000 bales, and Japan increased by 70,000 bales, but the United States decreased by 400,000 bales, China decreased by 60,000 bales, and other countries did not change much. The inventory of cotton for textiles in January of this year was higher than at the end of July last year. Except for Indian cotton, which decreased by 324,000 bales, American cotton, Egyptian cotton, and other types of cotton all increased, so the total increased by about 166,000 bales. If we look at each country separately, Japan decreased by 200,000 bales, India decreased by 110,000 bales, but the United States sharply increased by 250,000 bales, China increased by 72,000 bales, and Italy increased by 33,000 bales. As for the number of textile machines in use, at the end of January this year, it decreased by 124,000 spindles compared to the end of July last year, mainly due to the sharp decrease of 1,049,000 spindles in the United Kingdom. Other countries generally increased, but Japan alone increased by 432,000 spindles. In addition, from August of last year to January of this year, the working hours of textile mills in various countries (calculated on a 48-hour week) were more than in the previous period. The most notable were China and Japan. The list is as follows:
